  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ed173199-4734-428e-9526-e89f8ae8f4a4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText10196739591462426037" style="display:none"><i>A revenge that will consume her. A love that will ruin her.</i><br /><br />Emelina Flores has nothing. Her home in Ruina has been ravaged by war. She lacks the powers of her fellow Ruined. Worst of all, she witnessed her parents’ brutal murders and watched helplessly as her sister, Olivia, was kidnapped.<br /><br />But because Em has nothing, she has nothing to lose. Driven by a blind desire for revenge, Em sets off on a dangerous journey to the enemy kingdom of Lera. Somewhere within Lera’s borders, Em hopes to find Olivia. But in order to find her, Em must infiltrate the royal family.<br /><br />In a brilliant, elaborate plan of deception and murder, Em marries Prince Casimir, next in line to take Lera’s throne. If anyone in Lera discovers Em is not Casimir’s true betrothed, Em will be executed on the spot. But it’s the only way to salvage Em’s kingdom and what is left of her family.<br /><br />Em is determined to succeed, but the closer she gets to the prince, the more she questions her mission. Em’s rage-filled heart begins to soften. But with her life—and her family—on the line, love could be Em’s deadliest mistake.</span>

    I expected that too but surprisingly no, there is a second book and third on the way so i don't know about later but in this book she really doesn't have any magical powers. Her power is that other people's powers can't hurt her so i don't think she will have magical powers out of nowhere but like i said i can't be sure for the other two books.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471420371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer751341437934094053"><blockquote>
  <i>She slipped her hand into his, and when he laced their fingers together, her entire traitor body flushed. She ducked her head, pretending not to notice the bursts of happiness exploding in her chest.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This is absolutely nothing new.</b> Recycled characters and story, with a plot driven by romance.<br/><br/>Yes, part of the problem with this book is that it <b>feels so familiar</b>. Emelina Flores disguises herself as someone else and infiltrates the palace of her enemies (this also happens in some way in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_' title='Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Throne of</a></span>
  <span id="freeText751341437934094053" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She slipped her hand into his, and when he laced their fingers together, her entire traitor body flushed. She ducked her head, pretending not to notice the bursts of happiness exploding in her chest.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This is absolutely nothing new.</b> Recycled characters and story, with a plot driven by romance.<br /><br />Yes, part of the problem with this book is that it <b>feels so familiar</b>. Emelina Flores disguises herself as someone else and infiltrates the palace of her enemies (this also happens in some way in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a>). Despite being hardcore and all about revenge, she quickly gets caught up in <b>definitely not thinking about Cas</b>, and sashaying in front of the mirror in pretty dresses.<br /><br />But let's forget about all those identical books that have come before this for a second and view <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26074185.Ruined__Ruined___1_" title="Ruined (Ruined, #1) by Amy Tintera" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruined</a> on its own.<br /><br />Well, firstly, <b>the world-building is incredibly vague</b>. There are four kingdoms in this land and I have no idea where they are in relation to one another, what they're doing, what makes them different, and why everyone wants to kill the Ruined. Seriously, everyone hates them and we are never given a real reason.<br /><br />Emelina Flores is one of the Ruined and she wants to a) find out where the Lera king is holding her sister captive, and b) stop everyone from killing the Ruined. So she blows in with a sword, murders Princess Mary of Vallos, and assumes her identity so she can marry Prince Casimir of Lera and find the information she needs.<br /><br /><b>Infiltration!<br />Badassery!<br />Revenge!</b><br />Oh, wait.... is that a hot prince?<br /><br />And that's when our sword-wielding warrior heroine's plans come crumbling down beneath the <b>unconvincing romance</b>. For one thing, she goes from hating Cas to being all googly-eyed in almost no time at all. For another, Cas's personality is... virtually nonexistent. He seems to exist simply as a love interest for Emelina and every thought he has is either about her or influenced by what she says. <br /><br />It's like he never thought anything about anything until she puts ideas in his head. And also, <b>he's a little bit stupid</b>. Emelina is really not that good at being someone else, or at subtly finding out information. It's quite amazing that Cas never thinks something might be up when she openly sympathizes with the Ruined and literally comes out and asks where her sister is being kept. She's basically got "impostor" tattooed across her forehead.<br /><br />Almost as soon as it is introduced, the plot becomes driven by the romance. Other dramatic discoveries and events are only explored in relation to how this affects the relationship between Emelina and Cas. Side characters remain undeveloped, as do the world and wider politics.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26074185.Ruined__Ruined___1_" title="Ruined (Ruined, #1) by Amy Tintera" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruined</a> is a surface story with kissing and sword fights, reminiscent of other, often better, works. The ending is cliffhanger free, but still necessitates a sequel.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="751341437934094053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText10801465373983681050" style="display:none">I thought this book was bloody brilliant! It starts right off with the killing of some royals. Yay, lets start our revenge early =) I mean if you kill my family you best believe revenge is in your future. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499257004ra/23209874.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Em, Damien and Aren are on a quest to infiltrate the enemy in order to take said enemy out. <div id="review_1415363378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415363378" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1415363378?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781760290641" href="/book/show/28562419-ruined">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=foodie-fiction">foodie-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1415363378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5161288179200271993"><b>I am here to graciously update your (otherwise boring) day with the knowledge that: THIS BOOK IS BRILLIANT.</b> THE END! Hhahhahah. Just kidding. I have <i>so</i> much more to say than that. But I actually shut this book, looked at my dog and said, "So so so good." (FYI: my dog is uncultured swine and didn't care and just left the room. Do not be like my dog.)<br/><br/>I had a <i>feeling</i> I would adore this before I started because a) epic fantasy, and b) Amy Tintera. About 900 years ago Amy Tintera wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13517455.Reboot__Reboot___1_' title='Reboot (Reboot, #1) by Amy Tintera' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reboot</a> which I</span>
  <span id="freeText5161288179200271993" style="display:none"><b>I am here to graciously update your (otherwise boring) day with the knowledge that: THIS BOOK IS BRILLIANT.</b> THE END! Hhahhahah. Just kidding. I have <i>so</i> much more to say than that. But I actually shut this book, looked at my dog and said, "So so so good." (FYI: my dog is uncultured swine and didn't care and just left the room. Do not be like my dog.)<br /><br />I had a <i>feeling</i> I would adore this before I started because a) epic fantasy, and b) Amy Tintera. About 900 years ago Amy Tintera wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13517455.Reboot__Reboot___1_" title="Reboot (Reboot, #1) by Amy Tintera" rel="nofollow noopener">Reboot</a> which I FREAKING ADORED. So I basically will <b>emblazon upon my forehead that I am an Tintera fan.</b> I'll read whatever she writes. ABSOLUTELY. (Do we get a fandom name? Tintera Horde? Tinterai? Tinterathans? &lt;--- THAT ONE CLEARLY<br /><br /><b>EVERYTHING I LOVED ABOUT THIS BOOK:</b><br /><br />•<b> An epic world that was actually EPIC.</b><br />Excuse me, my name is Fussy. I read a lot of epic fantasy were the worlds are poorly built, but this? THIS WAS SO GOOD. (It was only missing a map, seriously...where was my map????) It managed to give me THREE races of people that all stood apart, didn't have confusing names, and had interesting and different cultures.<br /><br /><br />•<b> Let us just FLAIL for the morally grey!</b><br />Um, wait. That sounds bad. HERE ME OUT. I really love when their are races pitted against each other: but in Ruined <b>you honestly can't pick which is the "Good" side.</b> WHICH I LOOOOOVE. The magical people (the Ruined) are being hunted and killed by the Lera. But the Ruined are like TORTURERS and they're brutal as vicious killer whales. (More killer than whale though, fyi.) And then the Lera? They're all into colours and good times BUT THEY ARE VIOLENT AND UNFORGIVING TOO. The Lera King is <i>bad news</i>. <br /><br />So honestly everyone was evil and I am a fan.<br /><br /><br /><b>• We have the most adorable stabby cinnamon rolls of protagonists.</b><br />It's dual narrated by <b>Em</b> (who is actually non-magical BUT still a Ruined) and <b>Cas</b> (who is the future king of Lera). Em is like "STABBY STABBY" and Cas is like "NICEY NICEY" and hold me while <i>I adore them both so so much</i>. Em literally meets people, acts all polite, and meanwhile is plotting how to kill them. Like, don't we all? Totally. Cas is super NICE and also a wicked good swordsman and SO SARCASTIC I CANNOT EVEN WITH HIS ADORABLENESS.<br /><br />Naturally, Em is pretending to be someone else (in order to take down his kingdom) so she ends up married to him and HAHHAAHH. OH DEAR. They're basically doing the wedding dance and she's thinking how she could stab him. #shipit<br /><br /><br /><b>• Did I mention the SARCASM yet?????</b><br />Because I AM IN LOVE WITH SARCASM. AAAAALL THE SARCASM OMG. <b>The dialogue is perfectly ON POINT.</b> I laughed (out! loud!) several times and I just enjoyed how flawlessly the banter wove in with the tense moments and how perfectly dry Cas could be. It is my <i>favourite</i>. The sarcasm was LETHAL. I wanted to quote every bit of dialogue here, honestly.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>My wife didn't smother me with a pillow. Must be love!</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>• Okay so just let's face facts that this book is everything.</b><br />I had perfectly interesting plot. It managed to use a LOT of average-epic-fantasy-tropes and yet twist them to be unique. It gave us the cliche "tough female protagonist who don't need no man" but also made her super relatable and venerable. (Also she's on a quest to find her little sister!! SISTER GOALS!!) And it gave us the super nice prince who is a LITTLE BORED OF EVERYONE'S FACES but also entirely winning. The murder and mayhem were BIG. Like <b>blood is shed, folks, lots of blood, lots of shedding.</b> It didn't shy away from killing darlings. THERE IS TORTURE AND JUNGLES AND RUNNING AND BLEEDING AND SNEAKY KISSES. The romance never drowns the plot, but it's a gorgeous addition. And the magic is stunning and vicious. The Ruined can like split people from the inside out. <i>They are freaking awesome.</i><br /><br /><br /><b> Oh and the ending?</b><br />aHHHHHHHHH. BEST ENDING EVER. It's <i>nearly</i> a cliffhanger (I mean, it is) but it's also satisfying. And I'm 100000% in need of the next book. LIKE IT HAS OPENED ITSELF UP FOR SO MUCH AWESOME. Mad characters prevail. All the Ruined are gnashing their teeth and getting ready to pop skulls. THERE WILL BE WAR. I CANNOT WAIT.<br /><br /><br />...So basically <b>perfect book is perfect.</b> And my only <i>teeny tiny</i> comment is that Em and Cas were VERY like Wren/Callum from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13517455.Reboot__Reboot___1_" title="Reboot (Reboot, #1) by Amy Tintera" rel="nofollow noopener">Reboot</a>. But then. I adored <i>them</i> and I adore Em/Cas. SO. I ain't complaining.<br /><br /><b>GO READ THIS BOOK BASICALLY.</b> For everyone looking for a GOODLY EXCELLENT 2016 epic fantasy series? This is it.<br /><br /><br />**** QUOTES ****<br /><br /><blockquote>"Cheese bread," he said, handing one bag to her, and another to Galo. "Every time you come to the city, you buy one. It's a rule."<br />She opened the bag and peeked inside, the smell of fresh bread wafting through the air. She grabbed the bun and took a small bite. It was soft and chewy, with a hint of cheese flavour, and she took a second, bigger bite.<br />"It's delicious," she said.<br />"I'm glad you like it. The marriage might not have worked out if you didn't." The edges of Cas's mouth twitched.<br />"How tragic. The union between Lera and Vallos destroyed over cheese bread."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"If you take off his blindfold, he'll kill us all," Koldo said, shakily getting to his feet.<br />"Probably not," Aren said. "I'd say there's only like a sixty percent chance I kill you all."<br />"Aren," Em said in a warning tone.<br />He let out an exaggerated sigh. "Fine. Fifty percent."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>The king sighed. "I suppose you could've done worse than Mary."<br />"We should ask the priest to say that at the wedding," Cas said. "'And now we unite Casimir and Mary. They both could have done worse."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5161288179200271993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1581795936?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=revenge">revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581795936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2990048823867525644"><br/><strong>
  <em>Mary swung at her again, and Em grabbed her wrist, yanking the arm with the dagger to the sky.</em>
</strong><br/><strong>
  <em> With her other hand, Em drove the sword into the princess’s chest.</em>
</strong><br/><br/>It took five pages before I witnessed the heroine kill someone in cold blood.<br/><br/>That’s how long it took for her to awaken my interest.<br/><br/>And so when I read this following passage: <strong>
  <em>No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had ever known.</em>
</strong><br/><strong>
  <em> But they would.</em>
</strong><br/><br/>I believed every written word.<br/><br/>Emel</span>
  <span id="freeText2990048823867525644" style="display:none"><br /><strong>
  <em>Mary swung at her again, and Em grabbed her wrist, yanking the arm with the dagger to the sky.</em>
</strong><br /><strong>
  <em> With her other hand, Em drove the sword into the princess’s chest.</em>
</strong><br /><br />It took five pages before I witnessed the heroine kill someone in cold blood.<br /><br />That’s how long it took for her to awaken my interest.<br /><br />And so when I read this following passage: <strong>
  <em>No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had ever known.</em>
</strong><br /><strong>
  <em> But they would.</em>
</strong><br /><br />I believed every written word.<br /><br />Emelina wants revenge. Her home was destroyed, her parents murdered and her sister taken away. She has absolutely nothing left. Except… for a revenge plan! Her mission is to kill Prince Casimir Gallegos and the rest of his Royal family and strip the enemy’s kingdom of its power and stability.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>The king sighed. ‘‘I suppose you could have done worse than Mary.’’</em>
</strong><br /><strong>
  <em> ‘‘We should ask the priest to say that at the wedding,’’ Cas said. ‘‘And now we unite Casimir and Mary. They both could have done worse.’’</em>
</strong><br /><br />I like Amy Tintera’s humor, but for such a nasty and intense story, the amount of humor it contains is really too high. It functions in lightening the atmosphere, but the atmosphere isn’t meant to be light and there are even moments where humor doesn’t have any reason to be present.<br /><br />Emelina is a kickass heroine. She’s fearless, skilled in battle, strong… but human still. She’s not cold-heartened, as I first suspected, or pitiless. She’s the protector. She wants everyone she cares about to be safe, even at the expanse of others. She learned that from her mom, Wenda, the scariest queen that ever existed. I would give anything to never meet her.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Wenda smiled at Em. ‘‘Your sister is going to take that man’s head clean off his body. Would you like to come watch?’’</strong>
</em><br /><br />Terrifying person.<br /><br />So, really, except for the unnecessary overuse of humor, I immensely enjoyed the detailed world-building, the structured plot, the strong characters and the wonderful writing style.<br /><br />This is my <em>first</em> book by this author, but knowing me, I’ll be going straight to a bookstore to buy her Reboot duology ASAP.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/hitormissbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/hitormissbooks/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> </span>

    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684201745?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=bf">bf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684201745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3692645019434397526">Can Em teach me how to be as kickass as her please?? I want to slice and dice bitches with a sword too. 😍 This book was so fun!!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <u>What's it about???</u>
</blockquote><br/>Emelina Flores witnessed the brutal murder of her parents and her sister being kidnapped by the enemy kingdom, Lera. Her people, the <i>Ruined</i> are killed and hunted down every day for their magic and while she doesn't have magic herself, that doesn't make her any less powerful!! Wanting to rescue her sister and seek revenge, she forms a plan that incl</span>
  <span id="freeText3692645019434397526" style="display:none">Can Em teach me how to be as kickass as her please?? I want to slice and dice bitches with a sword too. 😍 This book was so fun!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>What's it about???</u>
</blockquote><br />Emelina Flores witnessed the brutal murder of her parents and her sister being kidnapped by the enemy kingdom, Lera. Her people, the <i>Ruined</i> are killed and hunted down every day for their magic and while she doesn't have magic herself, that doesn't make her any less powerful!! Wanting to rescue her sister and seek revenge, she forms a plan that includes marrying Prince Casimir, next in line for Lera's throne. Too bad he's hot.<br /><br />I liked this book, but honestly?? the plot line felt too familiar. Assassin/killer sent to butcher up someone or spy but ends up falling in <i>looooove</i> with who they're supposed to kill. I don't remember the exact titles, but there are definitely a lot of YA books with a similar plot out there.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>THE GOOD THINGS!</u>
</blockquote><br />●Our main character Emelina is such a badass. Get yourself a girl who knows her way with a sword and isn't afraid to slice up a bitch!!! She's so strong and kickass. The best part about it? It feels so natural and we aren't told 20 million times how badass she is. Her strength is shown in the action scenes and when she's training/practicing. Not only is she a kickass bitch, but she's nice, understanding, clever, smart and just not an asshole??? Which is so rare in YA. And we also have other kickass female warriors!!!<br /><br />●This book is really fast paced and easy to read. The writing is simple and enjoyable and kept me hooked.<br /><br />●Though the story is VERY familiar, it was actually pretty enjoyable??? I don't want to say to much because it'll become spoiler-y, but there is sort of a twist that took me by surprise and that's when shit went down and I was all like !!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! The action scenes were intense and had me screaming.<br /><br />●There's also a lot of murder and death and tbh, it's always appreciated in books for me!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>THE BAD THINGS!</u>
</blockquote><br />●I DIDN'T LIKE THEIR ROMANCE!!!! I know!!! It is supposed to be a romance, I mean, it literally says that in the blurb, but I THOUGHT IT WOULD BE WELL WRITTEN!!! It wasn't!!!!!! Their romance felt boring and I felt like there was 0 chemistry?? It just happened suddenly, idk felt bland. I don't really ship them, they're just such a boring couple together, ngl.<br /><br />●THE FIRST HALF WAS REALLY BORING. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A lot of it was Em's times spent in the castle, thinking about her feelings for Cas and planning, which was just really meh. I wanted the action, which I did get in the second half of the book, but the first half was still really boring and meh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, it was a fun book and the second half of this book really woke me up and had me hooked. Despite my problems, I enjoyed it and will definitely continue on with the series.<br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1651684893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1651684893" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1651684893?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1651684893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7079770308180842105"><blockquote>
  <i>❝No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had ever known.<br/>But they would.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Ruined was a quick read and I was glad I enjoyed most of it. I honestly couldn't put it down even though there were times where I just wanted to give up because nothing was happening. There was a pretty badass heroine, a great friendship that picked each other over anything else, the right amount of romance where nothing was rushed, and a prince who didn't quite enjoy being pri</span>
  <span id="freeText7079770308180842105" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had ever known.<br>But they would.❞</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Ruined was a quick read and I was glad I enjoyed most of it. I honestly couldn't put it down even though there were times where I just wanted to give up because nothing was happening. There was a pretty badass heroine, a great friendship that picked each other over anything else, the right amount of romance where nothing was rushed, and a prince who didn't quite enjoy being prince at times. Amy Tintera wrote this and to the ones who have read it, they can see similarities between this one and other novels. <i>A heroine who changes her identity in order to get back something they took from her.</i> Well that sounds familiar.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454702745i/18003021._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>You were born useless, but you don't have to be helpless.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Emelina Flores</b>, Em, really just wants revenge and to get her sister back, the one person she was supposed to protect but failed, leaving her alone because she was taken from her in front of her. Now that Em has become stronger and fierce, she's loyal to herself, telling herself she will save her sister and make them pay for what they have done. To try and save herself, she must keep her real identity safe and hidden and disguise herself as someone else. Maybe someone who looks like her in some ways or many ways and in ways where others wouldn't be able to tell them apart. Maybe someone like a princess.<br><br>That's what she does. Disguises her as Princess Mary, Mary who is supposed to marry the prince of Lera, the kingdom she wants to burn because of what they have taken from her. Princess Mary isn't just a princess. She killed Em's father (this isn't a spoiler it's in like page 5) so why not kill the person who killed your family member and left you alone, in pieces? Even though Mary knows she doesn't exactly look like Mary, she knows the Queen, King and Prince won't be able to tell. As she arrives, she's told to marry the prince and even though she knew this, she didn't want it but even with that, she blends in with everything and everyone, making it seem like she's been waiting for this moment.<br><br><b>Casimir Gallegos</b>, Cas, is quite surprised when he meets <i>Princess Mary.</i> Rumors spread saying she was beautiful in her own way and appealing, but <s>Em</s> Mary wasn't any of those. Even though he doesn't know what is really going on, Cas just goes along with it. He doesn't try much or hard to impress Mary since she doesn't show much care. She looked nervous and terrified when she arrived. She looked afraid but so did he. He looked afraid and terrified because he thought something was wrong and maybe Mary changed her mind or something. Well, something definitely was wrong, he just didn't know what.<br><br>As the two spend time together and act like a normal married couple would, they both end up falling for each other even when both didn't plan to. Mary is doing it for revenge, Cas is doing it because he was basically forced to. But even with the resisting feelings and trying to get away from each other, they both can't hide each others true identities when it comes to exposing themselves. And now that Cas knows who Mary really is and what is going on, all he wants to do is get his revenge. But how will he when he is so mad at this Emelina Flores when he is falling in love with her in ways he didn't know he could?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454702745i/18003021._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>The memory of how he felt when he cared about her was going to be the most painful thing after he began to hate her.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Ruined</i> is told in 2 perspectives, Em and Cas. She actually did a really good job keeping it in order and following the next. I enjoyed both perspectives even though Em's were a lot more entertaining and superior. They're both really different. Em is someone who can handle a sword a lot better than most guards at the castle and Cas is just known as someone who gets orders obeyed (sometimes) and isn't used to be attacked. I mean, isn't every prince? But even with that, I actually enjoyed both characters and none were annoying. They didn't get on my nerves or frustrate me in any way and I was glad Amy was able to get both to accept each other's failures and accept what is coming next. Her writing did remind me of Kiera Cass' writing. A little boring but at the same time it had its different way. It had less cheesy moments since Em is no America and Cas is no Maxon. The romance is a lot different but even with that, the format of the writing was a little similar but I actually enjoyed most of it here and there.<br><br>I must admit, Cas annoyed me in the beginning because he was known as a weak prince. It's no surprise where princess are weak and aren't used to being attacked or fighting, but sometimes I wish there was more development in them and they wouldn't turn out like their father. In most YA novels I read that deal with a Prince and King, the King is always rude, selfless, arrogant, and evil when the prince just wants everything to be better and doesn't want to be like his father. I was glad Cas wasn't like that but I was also hoping he would be able to fight a little more. Even though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his kingdom was taken down and his parents were killed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I expected him to be a litle stronger and maybe be able to fight more, maybe stand up to his own mother and tell her that he isn't the same child she's been used to spoiling and taking care of. But normally, whether it is the mother or father, they can't do much. They are afraid of what can happen or what control they can have over him. But even with that said, I wish Cas was a whole lot stronger and would be able to help Em instead of her helping him.<br><br>Now that I mention Em, she was pretty strong and fierce. She's known as other YA heroines that want to seek revenge so they do whatever it takes to earn it and take it, even if it means exposing their identity and letting every one know who they really are. Even if punishment known as death comes along the way. She showed herself as strong and competitive when it came to showing the King who is stronger. She was able to impress many people and I was glad she sticked to her plan the whole way eve when she had to witness things she never wished to see. Nothing from her change and I was actually glad because I didn't expect much from her. She went to the castle to get information about her sister and she left with it. She was able to reunite with her and I was glad she didn't turn out to be one of those heroines that decide to change their mind and move on to something else. She was honesty about her feelings for Cas and was honest about her own information. <br><br>As a conclusion, I've never heard of Amy Tintera and her writing. I've seen her other series at the library and not knowing she's the same author as this one, I didn't know much about it. I was gonna pick it up and see if I would enjoy the first book, but when it comes to libraries and staring at multiple shelves with YA books that you have heard of and have been dying to read, well, I think we all know what happens.<br><br><i>*ends up checking out unexpected amount of unexpected books.*</i><br><br>Overall, Amy's writing isn't cheesy but instead kind of gripping and I was glad I decided to pick this one up and see if I would enjoy it since not many have enjoyed it. I really want to read the other 2 and I know waiting is one of the hardest things to do, especially for next year and the year after but, we've all been there so I'm sure I can make it as well. It didn't really end with a cliffhanger but it did leave me with suspense and wanting more because with that ending, I'm pretty sure Em is gonna end up taking a throne of <i>the</i> throne. Not really sure since I don't even know if she wants to. She really just wanted to get her sister back, so I don't have any predictions or thoughts about the second book but I'm hoping she gets stronger and stronger and hopefully reunites with Cas because the romance in this was pretty slow, since it was a forced marriage and neither really <b>loved</b> each other. The ending was a little predictable and I kind of had it coming, but all I'm really hoping now is this kind of follows the same path as <i>The Young Elites</i> and Em just gets stronger, darker, and isn't afraid of anyone. She hasn't been afraid of anyone, so I can only imagine what is coming.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454702745i/18003021._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Cas returned from the jungle with a few round yellow fruits. His cheeks and the bridge of his nose were a bit pink from the sun, and it made him even cuter, if that was possible. And he'd taken his shirt off and slung it over his shoulder. Em found herself staring at one particular drop of water making a journey from the base of his throat down the center of his chest. She watched as it rolled down, sliding across his skin and disappearing into the ridges of his abdominals. She had never wanted to be a drop of water so badly.</i><br><br>I think I laughed too hard for too long at that quote.<br><br><b>“She had never wanted to be a drop of water so badly.”</b> OH MY GODSADSSD AMY</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7079770308180842105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1826551783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826551783" />
    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826551783?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826551783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5866145377072550509"><blockquote><b>**3.5 stars**<br/> I hate to spoil, but needs must.</b><br/><br/><b>This is a plot and character driven book told in a simple and linear manner.... unfortunately.</b> Sequential in it's telling, I could easily plot a graph of the story as each milestone and arc were unveiled<br/><br/>√ <i>Revenge plot. That'll be point one on said graph<br/><br/>√ Infiltrate enemy's camp. Point two<br/><br/>√ Discover the nice-looking boy who is an integral part of the enemy's camp<br/><br/>√ Reconnaissance <br/><br/>√ Develop feelings for said boy<br/><br/>√ Begin to doubt the rationale for the rev</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5866145377072550509" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>**3.5 stars**<br /> I hate to spoil, but needs must.</b><br /><br /><b>This is a plot and character driven book told in a simple and linear manner.... unfortunately.</b> Sequential in it's telling, I could easily plot a graph of the story as each milestone and arc were unveiled<br /><br />√ <i>Revenge plot. That'll be point one on said graph<br /><br />√ Infiltrate enemy's camp. Point two<br /><br />√ Discover the nice-looking boy who is an integral part of the enemy's camp<br /><br />√ Reconnaissance <br /><br />√ Develop feelings for said boy<br /><br />√ Begin to doubt the rationale for the revenge plot<br /><br />√ No chance of backtracking despite newly developed "feelings"<br /><br />√ Attack<br /><br />√ Escape<br /><br />√ Double back to complete the first part of the mission with help of a certain good-looking boy<br /><br />√ End of story.</i><br /><br />I haven't read a lot of dystopian books, so that might explain my ambivalence toward <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26074185-ruined" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruined</a>. It was tough getting invested in the story and not until I'd picked it up and set it aside a few times did it finally reel me in. <b>Emelina Flores, a Ruina princess, is out to avenge the death of her parents in addition to rescuing, Olivia, her abducted sister.</b> After a year of planning, she succeeds in infiltrating the enemy's camp by posing as the <b>young Prince Casimir's -of Lera- intended bride.<br /><br /></b> This is where I deducted a half star from my rating. <br /><br />For such an elemental part of this story, the ease with which Em could slip into the enemy's camp was unbelievable. That no one questioned her lack of- female- travel companions makes me wonder in which time period this was set. Regardless, it should have been expected that a princess would arrive with at minimum, one female maid/or equivalent. Another half point deducted.<br /><br />The author attempted to build the world of four kingdoms comprising Ruina, Lera, Vallos and Olso and while I didn't expect worldbuilding on the scale of say, Ketterdam in Six of Crows, I still would have appreciated a better description of the ambiance and atmosphere. Deduct half point.<br /><br />The characters were developed enough, with Em portrayed as the cold calculating strategist and, Cas, the naive and insulated prince. <b>The characterizations were authentic as neither protagonist was given too many unusual powers or authority.</b>Cas was still very much a boy albeit one with extensive sword and fighting skills while Em was, intermittently, subject to bouts of fear and doubt. These rang true and gave the author room to explore future growth.<br /><br /><b>Now on to the plot.</b> Ruina is a kingdom of people where some were born with special powers. Due to fear, prejudice, and ignorance, the kings of the other kingdoms colluded to eliminate the <b>RUINED</b>, leaving in their wake a grieving kingdom bent on revenge. I agree this theme/premise has been tackled successfully in other Dystopian/Fantasy books but much like the contemporary romance genre, I do believe an overused theme still has many ways in which to spin it, which the author did quite well, IMO. <br /><br />Overall, I liked the story and expect book 2 will have the author throwing in more intrigue, suspense, and other interesting characters. <br /> </blockquote></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060450916?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>

          marked it as dnf




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060450916" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8191939527721501454">I quite liked the author's previous SF duology, so it's disappointing to find this one so lacking in world-building and solid characterization. The book starts off with decent fight scenes, but otherwise there isn't much else that interested me in the beginning. I also can't quite grasp the tone; I <i>think </i>it's supposed to be slightly humorous? But I'm not sure. It felt very off-kilter and sort of silly (reminiscent of a lite dystopian bestseller that shall not be named), and the combination of mo</span>
  <span id="freeText8191939527721501454" style="display:none">I quite liked the author's previous SF duology, so it's disappointing to find this one so lacking in world-building and solid characterization. The book starts off with decent fight scenes, but otherwise there isn't much else that interested me in the beginning. I also can't quite grasp the tone; I <i>think </i>it's supposed to be slightly humorous? But I'm not sure. It felt very off-kilter and sort of silly (reminiscent of a lite dystopian bestseller that shall not be named), and the combination of modern/mannered-for-fantasy's-sake language felt awkward to me. <br /><br /><b>DNF</b> around 65 pages. Honestly, I guess I should've known better when I saw the setting is in a place called "Ruina." Here's hoping the author goes back to science fiction after she finishes this series...but who knows, there's definitely an enthusiastic audience for this sort of thing. But it's not me. <br /><br /><i>A finished copy was provided by the publisher for this review.</i></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17363715677319486579"><b> Full Review </b><br/><br/>Any book that has me shook at how fast I read them, deserves 5 stars.<br/><br/><b> What I liked </b><br/>- As I mentioned in one of my updates, I loved the trope represented in this: Girl (<b>Em</b>) hates boy (<b>Cas</b>) because of what boy and his family did to her family. Girl pretends to be the person betrothed to boy. Girl marries boy in order to destroy his country from the inside. Girl realizes boy is not bad. Girl falls for boy. Girl doesn’t know what to do next <br/><br/>- This book was fast-paced. I started reading a</span>
  <span id="freeText17363715677319486579" style="display:none"><b> Full Review </b><br /><br />Any book that has me shook at how fast I read them, deserves 5 stars.<br /><br /><b> What I liked </b><br />- As I mentioned in one of my updates, I loved the trope represented in this: Girl (<b>Em</b>) hates boy (<b>Cas</b>) because of what boy and his family did to her family. Girl pretends to be the person betrothed to boy. Girl marries boy in order to destroy his country from the inside. Girl realizes boy is not bad. Girl falls for boy. Girl doesn’t know what to do next <br /><br />- This book was fast-paced. I started reading and before I knew it, I was already like halfway done lol. There was never a dull moment. <br /><br />- I liked the characters. From the main ones to the side characters and I loved seeing them interact with each other<br /><br />- I loved the romance!! I love how it was kinda slow-burning but not too slow lol.<br /><br /><i>“ kind, reasonable, thoughtful. It wasn't love or an admission of wild, passionate feelings, but he realized he liked her three words more” </i> <br /><br />In some books I read, I often wonder why a girl likes a boy or vice versa, especially when it isn’t obvious (if the love interest is annoying) so I loved how Em actually said her reasons instead of just declaring her love, and I agreed with them!! <br /> <br />- I liked how this book had a different spin on the “she’s one of a kind” trope. Em is part of a kingdom that has people known as “ruined’. These people have special abilities. There is a subsection of these people, known as “useless”. Although they have ruined blood in them, they have no abilities. Em is one of these people but what she lacked in ability, she gained in swordsmanship. <br /><br />Overall, I loved this book and I recommend it to everyone 😊</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894231220?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781760290641" href="/book/show/28562419-ruined">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-rereads">2017-rereads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894231220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15044357056842448116"><b>
  <i>"No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had every known.<br/><br/>But they would."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I randomly stumbled across this book in my local Dymocks store and I had honestly never heard of it before. I thought the cover looked cool and I decided to read the blurb. I thought it sounded pretty cool so I bought it and I haven't touched it for about a month. However, I was on instagram two days ago and Amie Kaufman (co author of Illuminae) was talking about book recommen</span>
  <span id="freeText15044357056842448116" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"No one feared Emelina Flores, the useless daughter of the most powerful queen Ruina had every known.<br><br>But they would."</i>
</b><br><br>I randomly stumbled across this book in my local Dymocks store and I had honestly never heard of it before. I thought the cover looked cool and I decided to read the blurb. I thought it sounded pretty cool so I bought it and I haven't touched it for about a month. However, I was on instagram two days ago and Amie Kaufman (co author of Illuminae) was talking about book recommendations. She mentioned this book and I went 'hey I have that book! I'll read it next' and now the rest is history. <br><br>In Ruined we follow Em, whose entire family was taken from her and her people are being murdered and she is <b>out for revenge</b>. Sounds pretty typical doesn't it? Well it is. Nothing about this book is necessarily new or unique but it was honestly <b>
  <u>incredible</u>
</b>. This has definitely got to be one of the most fast paced stories I've ever read and I was honestly hooked from page one and <b>I could not put this book down.</b> It took me a whole day to watch a 40 minute lecture for University because I kept getting distracted by this book. This was honestly me reading this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491107790ra/22376386.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like I said before, we follow Em who is out for revenge after the murder of her parents and the abduction of her younger sister, Olivia. In light of these events, Em decides to murder the princess of Vallos, Mary, who is about to marry the Prince of Lera, Casimir. So, Em kills her and takes her place instead and infiltrates the castle and ends up actually marrying Cas. Her plan is simple: kill the entire royal family so the Ruined can return to power with the help of the Olso people. However, Em soon realises that Cas isn't as bad as she expected. <br><br>Sounds pretty cliche but <b>BEAR WITH ME</b>. What makes this story so incredible is the characters and the DIALOGUE! Also, the way this book is executed is just amazing. The writing is fast paced and flows - even when the POV changes mid page it makes so much sense and you can't get confused. Honestly, my only problem with this book is that there was no map. I like maps. I like to gauge distances that characters travel and I also like to visualise where these events take place. But that's such a tiny complaint! I've never read about characters so dang sarcastic. It's a dual POV of both Cas and Em and I honestly adored seeing both sides of their story. <br><br><b>
  <i>"If you take off his blindfold, hell kill us all."<br>"Probably not. I'd say there's only like a sixty perfect chance I'll kill you all."</i>
</b><br><br>It's a dual POV of both Cas and Em and I honestly adored seeing both sides of their story. I also <b>adore</b> seeing how each individual character reacts to each other and how their feelings slowly grow separately. I just love a dual POV ok. <br><br><b>
  <i>"My wife didn't smother me with a pillow! Must be love!"</i>
</b><br><br>Em's inner monologue is absolutely hilarious. She meets someone and acts all polite but really she's plotting how to kill them and how long it would take for her to murder and quickly escape. Meanwhile. Cas is a precious darling and I love seeing him slowly understand that the way his mother and father rule is so wrong. However, I also loved that no one was fully right in the way they go about things. If that makes sense. Basically, everyone is a bit morally grey. Em preaches that murder isn't needed, but Cas always reminds her that she has done those things herself. I just really enjoy politics in books. <br><br>Both characters are ridiculously lovable and they're just as good together as they are apart. Also I loved how the author built so much angst by pretty much always interrupting their intimate moments with someone TRYING TO KILL ONE OF THEM!! The dance at their wedding was probably my favourite scene and I honestly couldn't stop squealing.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I tried so hard not to fall for you and failed miserably."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491107790ra/22376387.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Overall, this book is fantastic. One of the best I've read in a while. It's stabby and brutal (legit someones HEART IS RIPPED RIGHT OUT OF THEIR CHEST WITH MAGIC - fucking incredible) while also being adorable and sarcastic. This is honestly such a hidden gem and <b>if you trust my recommendations in anyway, <u>please do yourself a favour and read this book.</u></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441459229ra/16112433.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15044357056842448116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1670866604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1670866604" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1670866604?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=badass">badass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=brs-done">brs-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1670866604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18421713627779347962"><i>If you ask me-</i><br/>This book is not as bad as the negative reviews are saying.<br/>It's also not nearly as good as the positive reviews claim. <br/>Which lands Ruined squarely in the <b>mediocre</b> category. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517867428i/25008976._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Emelina, our heroine, is the powerless heir to the fallen kingdom Ruina, which was once filled with the prideful magic users called the <i>Ruined</i>. Their neighboring kingdom Lera conspired to assassinate Em's family, kidnap her sister, and hunt as many remaining Ruined as possible.<br/>Em makes a daring plan to impersona</span>
  <span id="freeText18421713627779347962" style="display:none"><i>If you ask me-</i><br>This book is not as bad as the negative reviews are saying.<br>It's also not nearly as good as the positive reviews claim. <br>Which lands Ruined squarely in the <b>mediocre</b> category. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517867428i/25008976._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Emelina, our heroine, is the powerless heir to the fallen kingdom Ruina, which was once filled with the prideful magic users called the <i>Ruined</i>. Their neighboring kingdom Lera conspired to assassinate Em's family, kidnap her sister, and hunt as many remaining Ruined as possible.<br>Em makes a daring plan to impersonate the betrothed of Lera prince Casimir in order to save her sister and exact revenge. Things go south when she (rather predictably) falls head over ass in love with Cas. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517866223ra/25008921.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Em is the big positive in the book - she's a refreshing main character. Self-reliant and ruthless, she doesn't waste time pondering the past. Nor does she have qualms about doing whatever it takes to win back her kingdom. In the very first chapter, Em murders a princess then wears the clothes off her dead body. Talk about a power woman. <br><br>The biggest letdown of the book was the predictability. There are no surprises to be found in the plot. In dystopia-fantasy YA bingo, this book takes the cake. <br>Dead parents? Check.<br>Prince as love interest? Yep.<br>Disadvantaged heroine with an impossible mission? Uh huh. <br>People with special powers? Got it. <br>Pseudo-fascist regime? You betcha. <br>Star-crossed lovers trope? Ohhhh yes.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517867195i/25008965.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Along with the unoriginal story comes the ridiculous ease with which Em executes her mission. She impersonates some princess, and no one in Lera bothers to check whether the princess is who she say she is??? None of the royal family has even seen this woman before the literal wedding day. I find that hard to believe. <br>Then Em starts acting very suspiciously; openly defending the Ruined, constantly asking after her sister's whereabouts, publicly making friends with enemies of Lera. Nobody inquires after her strange actions because, apparently, they're all too enamored with her presence?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517867195i/25008966._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I don't buy it. In any realistic world, the jig would have been up within seconds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18421713627779347962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2175588990957856276">So, turns out I'm super shitty at getting to those "review to come" reviews. Oops? Almost two weeks later I am here to write this review and my brain is still completely <b>exploded</b> from this book. Do you ever read a book and honestly have no clue how to put your opinions in words? <br/><br/>That is me @ <i>Ruined</i>. <br/><br/>A kickass main character, a beyond awesome plotline and an even better romance. Honestly, I adored this book. When a character is willing to murder someone in the opening pages <b>I am on board</b>. <br/><br/>There's</span>
  <span id="freeText2175588990957856276" style="display:none">So, turns out I'm super shitty at getting to those "review to come" reviews. Oops? Almost two weeks later I am here to write this review and my brain is still completely <b>exploded</b> from this book. Do you ever read a book and honestly have no clue how to put your opinions in words? <br /><br />That is me @ <i>Ruined</i>. <br /><br />A kickass main character, a beyond awesome plotline and an even better romance. Honestly, I adored this book. When a character is willing to murder someone in the opening pages <b>I am on board</b>. <br /><br />There's honestly not a lot I can say about this book without giving it away. There is no love triangle. There is murder. There is amazing characters. I beg you to pick it up. The writing is easy and quick to get through. I honestly couldn't put this book down. Highly recommend it and highly recommend Caitlin in general for recommendations because she is the book queen, lets be real. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9739729546381575151">*Full review update*<br/>Thumbs up, Amy Tintera, keep doing your thang. This was the perfect weekend read for me...<br/><br/>Cute, light weight, fast read- and pretty stinking adorable. Alright whatever maybe I'm referring to a certain character but don't judge k thanks. <br/><br/>So Ruined is definitely up my alley.<br/><br/><b>Castles?</b> Check. <br/><b>Magic?</b> Check<br/><b>Badass Heroine?</b> Check.<br/><b>Prince?</b> Check.<br/><b>Battles/action/wars?</b> Check.<br/><br/>The above is pretty much my standard <u>'Brittney recipe of success'</u> on whether or not I'm going to enjoy a book... so </span>
  <span id="freeText9739729546381575151" style="display:none">*Full review update*<br />Thumbs up, Amy Tintera, keep doing your thang. This was the perfect weekend read for me...<br /><br />Cute, light weight, fast read- and pretty stinking adorable. Alright whatever maybe I'm referring to a certain character but don't judge k thanks. <br /><br />So Ruined is definitely up my alley.<br /><br /><b>Castles?</b> Check. <br /><b>Magic?</b> Check<br /><b>Badass Heroine?</b> Check.<br /><b>Prince?</b> Check.<br /><b>Battles/action/wars?</b> Check.<br /><br />The above is pretty much my standard <u>'Brittney recipe of success'</u> on whether or not I'm going to enjoy a book... so I was destined to like this one.<br /><br />The plot was a little cliche, but who cares. If you know what you like, stick to it. Nothing super original in my opinion, but engaging nonetheless. Cmon, who doesn't want to read about a princess in disguise (mind you- who the world thinks is dead..) going to the country that destroyed her own in order to rescue her kidnapped sister and bring the country down to its knees from within? Lets leave it at that. Its a fun story! <br /><br />Ok ok ok but... <br /><br />I didn't have a ton of feels in this one (save for a few great moments) but I highly anticipate that to change as the series continues. The romance was light and sweet- though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I kinda wished they hated each other for longer... you know.. I like being tortured a it;)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But whatever. Lets see what happens.<br /><br />So overall, I liked it, and I'll definitely continue - and I recommend this to anyone looking for a fun whimsical read.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_1457070455" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1457070455" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1457070455?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fell-short-of-expectations">fell-short-of-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=generic-characters">generic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=clich%C3%A9">cliché</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=eye-rolling">eye-rolling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=multi-pov">multi-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=snark-i-am-coming">snark-i-am-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=pretty-cover-bad-execution">pretty-cover-bad-execution</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1457070455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17373639386654405284"><p><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br/><i><blockquote>Make people fear you, Emelina. Her mother’s words echoed in her head. Stop worrying about what you don’t have and start focusing on what you do. Make people tremble when they hear your name. Fear is your power.</blockquote></i><br/>Sorry to disappoint you Mom, but, well, fear and Emilina are not compatible. One moment the girl's a highly trained assassin, the next moment she's an uncertain girl who barely knows what to do with her body. This constant state of ambivalence got on my nerves quick</p></span>
  <span id="freeText17373639386654405284" style="display:none"><p><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br /><i><blockquote>Make people fear you, Emelina. Her mother’s words echoed in her head. Stop worrying about what you don’t have and start focusing on what you do. Make people tremble when they hear your name. Fear is your power.</blockquote></i><br />Sorry to disappoint you Mom, but, well, fear and Emilina are not compatible. One moment the girl's a highly trained assassin, the next moment she's an uncertain girl who barely knows what to do with her body. This constant state of ambivalence got on my nerves quickly: when you can't understand what the MC is made of and changes faces quicker than you can blink. I really tried to understand Em, but she barely understood herself if at all. It's not a case where a person is trying to find her true self, no, it's the case where author gave her character a personality but forgot to concretize how that personality operates. In other words: <b>underdeveloped</b>. The only thing I liked about Em is how every time she entered a room, she counted ways to kill people in it:<br /><i><blockquote>There was one knife on the tray, and Em studied it, trying to judge how sharp it was. Three quick steps across the room and she could reach around Davina for the knife to jab it in her throat before she knew what was happening. Five seconds, tops.</blockquote></i><br />But in the context of the book, this skill looks like a joke, because it feels like characters are playing games they don't understand. Kids got swords and knives and they are plunging them into enemies' (?) bodies, but it looks like <b>kids are playing war in a sandbox</b>. They don't really understand what they are doing, they simply have fun, because it's hilarious. <br /></p><p>Cas - the hero of the book is a blank page anyone can fill as they wish. He doesn't have a personality; he acts regarding other people's wishes. He doesn't have an opinion about a war that is raging on in his Kingdom for years now. When Em appears and starts to sympathize with the enemy, Cas doesn't think it's suspicious. He easily gives her secret military information, because he trusts her. Seriously? The prince is supposedly the best swardman in the Kingdom, but it seems he never made a step out of his sandbox. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Em's cover was blown and she ran, Cas chased after her, all he wanted to know is her name. Seriously?! How clever or strategic that is? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Again, I blame this on author and the <b>lack of character development</b>. <br /></p><p>The romance was... dull. I want to blame insta-love, but I've encountered insta-love in books before and in some of those book it was processed quite believably. Here everything is so rushed (not only romance but action either) I didn't have time to feel anything toward characters or notice when and how they developed feelings for each other. Whether they die or live, I don't care.<br /><i><blockquote>“You could at least pretend to be excited.”</blockquote></i><br />I tried, I really did. This book was on my list of highly anticipated releases, and I was sure I'll like it. But when there's no depth to plot or characters, it's hard to make oneself feel. This book is simply generic: been there, done that. Nothing new. It's not bad either (compared to my disappointment with ACOMAF, everything is better), there were nice moments, when it felt like one more page and I'll like the book. Alas, I reached the end but that feeling never came. I blinked, closed the book and forgot about the story.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="17373639386654405284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
